      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_media">Mass media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Mass media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mass_media_in_Turkmenistan" title="Mass media in Turkmenistan">Mass media in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Turkmenistan" title="Telecommunications in Turkmenistan">Telecommunications in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Newspapers and monthly magazines are published by state-controlled media outlets, primarily in <a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a>. The daily official newspaper is published in both Turkmen (<i>Türkmenistan</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> and Russian <a href="/wiki/Neytralny_Turkmenistan" title="Neytralny Turkmenistan">(<i>Нейтральный Туркменистан</i>)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Two online news portals repeat official content, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenportal" title="Turkmenportal">Turkmenportal</a> and Parahat.info,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> in addition to the official "Golden Age" (<a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a>: <span lang="tk">Altyn Asyr</span>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Золотой век</span>) news website,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> which is available in Turkmen, Russian, and English. Two Ashgabat-based private news organizations, Infoabad<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> and Arzuw,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> offer online content. </p>
      <p>Articles published by the state-controlled newspapers are heavily censored and written to glorify the state and its leader. Uncensored press coverage specific to Turkmenistan is provided only by news organizations located outside Turkmenistan: Azatlyk Radiosy,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> the Turkmen service of <a href="/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty" title="Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty">Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>; Chronicles of Turkmenistan,<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> the Vienna-based outlet of the Turkmen Initiative for Human Rights; Turkmen.news,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> previously known as Alternative News of Turkmenistan, based in the Netherlands; and Gündogar.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> In addition, Mediazona Central Asia,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Eurasianet<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> and Central Asia News<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> provide some reporting on events in Turkmenistan. </p>
      <p>Turkmenistan currently broadcasts 7 national TV channels via satellite. They are <a href="/wiki/Altyn_Asyr_(TV_channel)" title="Altyn Asyr (TV channel)">Altyn Asyr</a>, Ýaşlyk, <a href="/wiki/Miras_(TV_channel)" title="Miras (TV channel)">Miras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_(TV_channel)" title="Turkmenistan (TV channel)">Turkmenistan</a> (in 7 languages), <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmen_Owazy" title="Türkmen Owazy">Türkmen Owazy</a> (music), Aşgabat and <a href="/wiki/Sport_(Turkmen_TV_channel)" title="Sport (Turkmen TV channel)">Turkmenistan Sport</a>. There are no commercial or private TV stations. The nightly official news broadcast, <i>Watan</i> (Homeland), is available on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="infobox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.5em 1.5em">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <th colspan="2" class="infobox-above" style="font-size:115%">External video</th>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data" style="text-align: left"><img alt="video icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128"> Example of Turkmenistan TV News<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data" style="text-align: left"><img alt="video icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="128"> Turkmen President celebrates Independence Day<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Although officially banned,<sup id="cite_ref-at20150422_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-at20150422-85">[85]</a></sup> widespread use of satellite dish receivers allows access to foreign programming, particularly outside Ashgabat.<sup id="cite_ref-virusbashi_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-virusbashi-197">[197]</a></sup> Due to the high mutual intelligibility of the Turkmen and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish languages</a>, Turkish-language programs have grown in popularity despite official efforts to discourage viewership.<sup id="cite_ref-sat_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sat-198">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sat2_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sat2-199">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sat3_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sat3-200">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sat4_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sat4-201">[201]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Internet services are the least developed in Central Asia. Access to Internet services is provided by the government's <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_provider" title="Internet service provider">ISP</a> company, Turkmentelekom. As of 27 January 2021, Turkmenistan reported an estimated 1,265,794 internet users or roughly 21% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-World_Factbook_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Factbook-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays">Holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Turkmenistan" title="Public holidays in Turkmenistan">Public holidays in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Holidays in Turkmenistan are laid out in the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Turkmenistan" title="Constitution of Turkmenistan">Constitution of Turkmenistan</a>, Holidays in Turkmenistan practiced internationally include <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">New Year's Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nowruz" title="Nowruz">Nowruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Fitr" title="Eid al-Fitr">Eid al-Fitr</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a>. Turkmenistan exclusive holidays include <a href="/wiki/Melon_Day" title="Melon Day">Melon Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Women%27s_Day" title="International Women's Day">Turkmen Woman's Day</a>, and the Day of Remembrance for Saparmurat Niyazov. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Turkmenistan" title="Education in Turkmenistan">Education in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_(251).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg/220px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg/330px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg/440px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28251%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_(251).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Turkmeni students in university uniform
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education is universal and mandatory through the secondary level. Under former President Niyazov, the total duration of primary and secondary education was reduced from 10 to 9 years. President Berdimuhamedov restored 10-year education as of the 2007–2008 school year. Effective 2013, secondary general education in Turkmenistan was expanded to three-stages lasting 12 years: elementary school (grades 1–3), high school – the first cycle of secondary education with duration of 5 years (grades 4–8), and secondary school (grades 9–12).<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the end of the 2019–20 academic year, nearly 80,000 Turkmen pupils graduated from high school.<sup id="cite_ref-grads2020_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grads2020-206">[206]</a></sup> As of the 2019–20 academic year, 12,242 of these students were admitted to institutions of higher education in Turkmenistan. An additional 9,063 were admitted to the country's 42 vocational colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-mfaeduc_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfaeduc-207">[207]</a></sup> An estimated 95 thousand Turkmen students were enrolled in institutions of higher education abroad as of Autumn 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-foreign_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foreign-208">[208]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat#Architecture" title="Ashgabat">Ashgabat §&nbsp;Architecture</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The tasks for modern Turkmen architecture are diverse application of modern aesthetics, the search for an architect's own artistic style, and inclusion of the existing historico-cultural environment. Most major new buildings, especially those in <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat" title="Ashgabat">Ashgabat</a>, are faced with white <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">marble</a>. Major projects such as <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_Tower" title="Turkmenistan Tower">Turkmenistan Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wedding_Palace_(Ashgabat)" title="Wedding Palace (Ashgabat)">Bagt köşgi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alem_Cultural_and_Entertainment_Center" title="Alem Cultural and Entertainment Center">Alem Cultural and Entertainment Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat_Flagpole" title="Ashgabat Flagpole">Ashgabat Flagpole</a> have transformed the country's skyline and promote its identity as a modern, contemporary city. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Turkmenistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports in Turkmenistan">Sports in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The most popular sport in Turkmenistan is <a href="/wiki/Soccer" class="mw-redirect" title="Soccer">soccer</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_national_football_team" title="Turkmenistan national football team">national team</a> has never qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> but has appeared twice at the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">AFC Asian Cup</a>, in <a href="/wiki/2004_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2004 AFC Asian Cup">2004</a> and <a href="/wiki/2019_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2019 AFC Asian Cup">2019</a>, failing to advance past the group stage at both editions. Another popular sport is <a href="/wiki/Archery" title="Archery">archery</a>, Turkmenistan holds league and local competitions for archery. International sports events hosted in Turkmenistan include; the <a href="/wiki/2021_UCI_Track_Cycling_World_Championships" title="2021 UCI Track Cycling World Championships">2021 UCI Track Cycling World Championships</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2017_Asian_Indoor_and_Martial_Arts_Games" title="2017 Asian Indoor and Martial Arts Games">2017 Asian Indoor and Martial Arts Games</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2018_World_Weightlifting_Championships" title="2018 World Weightlifting Championships">2018 World Weightlifting Championships</a> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Turkmenistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation in Turkmenistan">Transportation in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Automobile_transport">Automobile transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Automobile transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Prior to the 1917 <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> only three automobiles existed in Turkmenistan, all of them foreign models in Ashgabat. No automobile roads existed between settlements. After the revolution, Soviet authorities graded dirt roads to connect Mary and Kushky (Serhetabat), Tejen and Sarahs, Kyzyl-Arvat (Serdar) with Garrygala (Magtymguly) and Chekishler, i.e., with important border crossings. In 1887-1888 the Gaudan Highway (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Гауданское шоссе</span>) was built between Ashgabat and the Persian border at Gaudan Pass, and Persian authorities extended it to Mashad, allowing for easier commercial relations. Municipal bus service began in Ashgabat in 1925 with five routes, and taxicab service began in 1938 with five vehicles. The road network was extended in the 1970s with construction of republic-level highways connecting Ashgabat and Kazanjyk (Bereket), Ashgabat and Bayramaly, Nebit Dag (Balkanabat) and Krasnovodsk (Turkmenbashy), Çärjew (Turkmenabat) and Kerki, and Mary and Kushka (Serhetabat).<sup id="cite_ref-encyc3_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyc3-209">[209]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The primary west–east motor route is the <a href="/wiki/M37_highway_(Turkmenistan)" title="M37 highway (Turkmenistan)">M37</a> highway linking the <a href="/wiki/Turkmenbashi_International_Seaport" title="Turkmenbashi International Seaport">Turkmenbashy International Seaport</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Farap" title="Farap">Farap</a> border crossing via Ashgabat, Mary, and Turkmenabat. The primary north–south route is the Ashgabat-Dashoguz Automobile Road (<a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a>: <span lang="tk">Aşgabat-Daşoguz awtomobil ýoly</span>), built in the 2000s. Major international routes include <a href="/wiki/European_route_E003" title="European route E003">European route E003</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_route_E60" title="European route E60">European route E60</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_route_E121" title="European route E121">European route E121</a>, and Asian Highway (AH) routes AH5, AH70, AH75, AH77, and AH78.<sup id="cite_ref-ah_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ah-210">[210]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A new toll motorway is under construction between Ashgabat and Turkmenabat by “Turkmen Awtoban” company, which will construct the 600-km highway in three phases: Ashgabat-Tejen by December 2020, Tejen-Mary by December 2022 and Mary-Turkmenabat by December 2023. A sister project to link Turkmenbashy and Ashgabat was suspended when the Turkish contractor, <a href="/wiki/Polimeks" title="Polimeks">Polimeks</a>, walked away from the project, reportedly because of non-payment.<sup id="cite_ref-doc_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doc-211">[211]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 29 January 2019, the Turkmen Automobile Roads state concern (<a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a>: <span lang="tk">Türkmenawtoýollary</span>) was subordinated by presidential decree to the Ministry of Construction and Architecture, and responsibility for road construction and maintenance was shifted to provincial and municipal governments.<sup id="cite_ref-decree_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-decree-212">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-roads_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roads-213">[213]</a></sup> Operation of motor coaches (buses) and taxicabs is the responsibility of the Automobile Services Agency (<a href="/wiki/Turkmen_language" title="Turkmen language">Turkmen</a>: <span lang="tk">Türkmenawtoulaglary Agentligi</span>) of the Ministry of Industry and Communication.<sup id="cite_ref-awtoulag_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awtoulag-214">[214]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">Air transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Air transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Turkmenistan" title="List of airports in Turkmenistan">List of airports in Turkmenistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Turkmenistan_Airlines_destinations" title="List of Turkmenistan Airlines destinations">List of Turkmenistan Airlines destinations</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg/220px-Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg/330px-Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg/440px-Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="895"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmenistan_Boeing_767-300ER_Simon-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_Airlines" title="Turkmenistan Airlines">Turkmenistan Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a>-300ER
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Air service began in 1927 with a route between Çärjew (Turkmenabat) and Tashauz (Dashoguz), flying German Junkers 13 and Soviet K-4 aircraft, each capable of carrying four passengers. In 1932 an aerodrome was built in Ashgabat on the site of the current Howdan neighborhoods, for both passenger and freight service, the latter mainly to deliver supplies to sulfur mines near Derweze in the Karakum Desert.<sup id="cite_ref-encyc2_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyc2-215">[215]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Airports serving the major cities of <a href="/wiki/Ashgabat" title="Ashgabat">Ashgabat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dashoguz" class="mw-redirect" title="Dashoguz">Dashoguz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Turkmenistan" title="Mary, Turkmenistan">Mary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenabat" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkmenabat">Turkmenabat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkmenbashy" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkmenbashy">Turkmenbashy</a>, which are operated by Turkmenistan's civil aviation authority's airline, Türkmenhowaýollary, feature scheduled domestic commercial air service.<sup id="cite_ref-schedule_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-216">[216]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thy_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thy-217">[217]</a></sup> Under normal circumstances international scheduled commercial air service is limited to Ashgabat. During the COVID-19 pandemic, however, international flights take off from and land at Turkmenabat, where quarantine facilities have been established.<sup id="cite_ref-state_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state-218">[218]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-karantin_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-karantin-219">[219]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>State-owned <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan_Airlines" title="Turkmenistan Airlines">Turkmenistan Airlines</a> is the only Turkmen air carrier. Turkmenistan Airlines' passenger fleet is composed solely of <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> Air transport carries more than two thousand passengers daily in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> Under normal conditions, international flights annually transport over half a million people into and out of Turkmenistan, and Turkmenistan Air operates regular flights to <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amritsar" title="Amritsar">Amritsar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lviv" title="Lviv">Lviv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a>. </p>
      <p>Small airfields serve industrial sites near other cities, but do not feature scheduled commercial passenger service. Airfields slated for modernization and expansion include those serving <a href="/wiki/Garabogaz" title="Garabogaz">Garabogaz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kerki" title="Kerki">Kerki</a>, Jebel, and <a href="/wiki/Gala%C3%BDmor" title="Galaýmor">Galaýmor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-airport_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airport-222">[222]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-galay_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-galay-223">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kerki_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kerki-224">[224]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gbogaz_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gbogaz-225">[225]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jebel2_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jebel2-226">[226]</a></sup> The new <a href="/wiki/Turkmenabat_International_Airport" title="Turkmenabat International Airport">Turkmenabat International Airport</a> was commissioned in February 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-tbat_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tbat-227">[227]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maritime_transport">Maritime transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Maritime transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_(314).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg/220px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg/330px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg/440px-Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_%28314%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4208" data-file-height="2795"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Independence_Day_Parade_-_Flickr_-_Kerri-Jo_(314).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Workers in the service of Maritime and River Transport of Turkmenistan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 1962, the <a href="/wiki/Turkmenbashi_International_Seaport" title="Turkmenbashi International Seaport">Turkmenbashy International Seaport</a> has operated a passenger ferry to the port of <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> as well as rail ferries to other ports on the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> (Baku, <a href="/wiki/Aktau" title="Aktau">Aktau</a>). In recent years tanker transport of oil to the ports of Baku and Makhachkala has increased. </p>
      <p>In May 2018 construction was completed of a major expansion of the Turkmenbashy seaport.<sup id="cite_ref-Turkmenistan_Transportation_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turkmenistan_Transportation-228">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> Cost of the project was $1.5 billion. The general contractor for the project was Gap Inşaat, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/%C3%87al%C4%B1k_Holding" title="Çalık Holding">Çalık Holding</a> of Turkey. The expansion added 17 million tons of annual capacity, making total throughput including previously existing facilities of over 25 million tons per year. The international ferry and passenger terminals will be able to serve 300,000 passengers and 75,000 vehicles per year, and the container terminal is designed to handle 400,000 TEU (20-foot container equivalent) per year.<sup id="cite_ref-enr_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enr-230">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-press_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-press-231">[231]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-trend_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trend-232">[232]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway_transport">Railway transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Railway transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg/220px-Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg/330px-Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg/440px-Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="964" data-file-height="770"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turkmen_Diesel_locomotive2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Turkmen Diesel locomotive
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Turkmenistan" title="Rail transport in Turkmenistan">Rail transport in Turkmenistan</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmendemir%C3%BDollary" title="Türkmendemirýollary">Türkmendemirýollary</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The first rail line in Turkmenistan was built in 1880, from the eastern shore of the Caspian Sea to Mollagara. By October 1881 the line was extended to <a href="/wiki/Serdar_(city)" title="Serdar (city)">Kyzyl-Arvat</a>, by 1886 had reached <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmenabat" title="Türkmenabat">Çärjew</a>. In 1887 a wooden rail bridge was built over the <a href="/wiki/Amu_Darya" title="Amu Darya">Amu Darya</a>, and the line was continued to <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a> (1888) and <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a> (1898).<sup id="cite_ref-encyc_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyc-233">[233]</a></sup> Rail service in Turkmenistan began as part of Imperial Russia's <a href="/wiki/Trans-Caspian_railway" title="Trans-Caspian railway">Trans-Caspian Railway</a>, then of the Central Asian Railway. After the <a href="/wiki/Collapse_of_the_USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Collapse of the USSR">collapse of the USSR</a>, the railway network in Turkmenistan was transferred to and operated by state-owned <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmendemir%C3%BDollary" title="Türkmendemirýollary">Türkmendemirýollary</a>. Rail gauge is the standard Russian- and Soviet 1520 millimeters. </p>
      <p>The total length of railways is 3181&nbsp;km. Only domestic passenger service is available, except for special trains operated by tour operators.<sup id="cite_ref-schedule2_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schedule2-234">[234]</a></sup> The railway carries approximately 5.5 million passengers and moves nearly 24 million tons of freight per year.<sup id="cite_ref-stat2020_99-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat2020-99">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rr_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rr-235">[235]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tour_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tour-236">[236]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Turkmen Railways is currently constructing a rail line in Afghanistan to connect <a href="/wiki/Serhetabat" title="Serhetabat">Serhetabat</a> to <a href="/wiki/Herat" title="Herat">Herat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-herat_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-herat-237">[237]</a></sup> Upon completion, it may connect to the proposed rail line to connect Herat to <a href="/wiki/Khaf,_Iran" title="Khaf, Iran">Khaf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-khaf_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khaf-238">[238]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Turkmenistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright"> 
       <ul> 
        <li><span><a href="/wiki/File:Asia_(orthographic_projection).svg" class="image"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Asia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/28px-Asia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="28" height="28" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Asia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/42px-Asia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Asia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/56px-Asia_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="541" data-file-height="541"></a></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Asia" title="Portal:Asia">Asia portal</a></span></li>
